Chunqiu

Tidbits 175

— (Xu Xiaoting)

On the vast wilderness, without sowing excellent seeds, you cannot get a full harvest. In the vast sea of people, without seeking profound knowledge, you cannot create outstanding careers.

Without great courage, how can you make people believe? Without excellent achievements, how can you make history remember your name? The environment can change life, and life can also change the environment. Fearing difficulties and living in ease can only hover around the environment, while striving and being brave can jump out of the environment to do things.

Looking at the great men in history, they only employed fate, but were not employed by fate. Life is not for enjoyment, but to leave some historical traces on the extremely ordinary process that future generations admire.

The earth is constantly rotating, and life on the earth's crust is growing peacefully. Friends of the leisure class are rotten seeds on the earth's crust, while hard-working and hard-working young people are full grains.

Society is decadent, life is moldy, those who enjoy life still enjoy life, and those who fear difficulties and live in ease are still fearing difficulties and living in ease. This pitiful parasitic life will eventually collapse and break. Revitalize, transform, and remedy. We do not want to hope for people to help, we must find ways to save ourselves.

Hero 176

— Hualing

Westerners were mocked as barbarians by the Chinese decades ago because Westerners are worshipers of heroism. Hunters, knights, and even pirates are regarded as heroes. At that time, our China was still a land of culture. Military officials of the same rank had to crawl on the ground and kowtow when they saw civil officials. All professions are inferior, only reading is high. Only those who are gentle and refined are the children of scholarly families. Those with big fists and thick arms are either peddlers or unruly rogues.

Today, heroism has raised its head and knocked open the door of the land of culture. Then everyone knows that the Mongolian-style knightly demeanor is what young people should have. Pale-faced, hunched-over scholars may be able to sweep away five thousand people with their pen tips, but this is just empty talk on paper and is not popular. Only young people with the Mongolian-style knightly demeanor can shoulder the heavy responsibility of reviving the nation.

China was never a land of culture in the first place. In ancient times, our ancestors also drank blood and conquered poisonous snakes and beasts, and also conquered the late-developing Chi You. Since the Zhou Dynasty, history has told us that the founding emperors of all dynasties did not obtain the world by wielding pens. Those who obtained the world all came from carrying guns. At the same time, any dynasty that wants to maintain the ancestral foundation must not fail to cultivate military preparations. Only by cultivating military preparations can they suppress rebellions internally and conquer strong neighbors externally. The last emperors are always good gentlemen who only know how to write poetry and compose lyrics. Strength overcomes softness. This is the supreme principle of physical examination. The rise and fall of a country and nation naturally cannot escape such a formula. In this era, everyone should realize that this is no longer an era of governing the world by yielding and persuading.

The ancient saying says, "Success makes you a king, failure makes you a bandit." Whether you become a king or a bandit, you are always a hero in the end. Although Napoleon was defeated and his career was not successful, Napoleon is recognized as a hero in history by anyone. Although Wilhelm II was defeated and exiled to an isolated island, he is still one of the heroes. Recently, heroism has permeated the entire earth. According to what history tells us, only nations with heroism have the hope of developing and growing. Everyone, work hard, only heroes can stand upright and survive. What we need now are young people with Mongolian knight-style, big fists, thick arms, who can bear the responsibility of defending the country.

Standard Husband 177

— Rong Yu

"Enduring hardship and hardship himself, only seeking happiness and enjoyment for his wife." This kind of standard husband can often be found in our human group, but it is difficult to find in other animals. Because many male animals, in addition to fulfilling the responsibilities of a husband during mating and reproduction, generally adhere to the principle of not hearing or asking about other things. So I often tell my friends in a literary way: "The reason why humans are different from animals is that husbands can fulfill their responsibilities to their wives." However, I have recently seen two things that have broken this statement, because there are also standard husbands among animals. If you don't believe it, look at the following:

A certain friend's house has a pair of monkeys, which are matched according to the current system of monogamy, so they lean on each other every day and can be called "virtuous couple." Later, the female monkey did not have a menstrual cycle, and her belly swelled, looking like she was going to have a son. At that time, the male monkey kept watch by her side, peeling fruits for her, catching fleas, and doing everything to serve her diligently. Later, the little monkey was born, and in addition to breastfeeding, the mother monkey, that monkey father, really fulfilled many responsibilities. I think at this time, the monkey wife must be happy that her husband can serve and be loyal!

Recently, I bought a pair of pigeons at the Yimiao and counted myself lucky. In just a few days, the female pigeon actually hatched a pair of small eggs. It is usually seen that in birds, hatching eggs is always the responsibility of the female, but what about the pigeons? Both sides share the burden, and the male pigeon takes up more of the hatching time. Later, the little pigeons came out. For the first half month, they could not peck food by themselves, and their father had to vomit the food he had eaten from his throat to feed the children; while the pigeon wife was very carefree, washing her feathers in the sun, preparing to make a splash!

The Mooncake's Fate 178

— Zhiyun

Who invented the mooncake, a thing filled with sweet stuffing, I don't know, but its significance is truly profound, reaching 120 points. It seems that many years ago, it was foreseen that every young man and woman would love a "Sweet Heart," which isn't that strange.

The mooncake symbolizes lovers, which is indeed very apt. However, in modern love unions, almost eight or nine out of ten inevitably end up on the path of a bitter end. The so-called sweetness is only an ideal during the courtship phase and a fleeting feeling in the early stages of marriage. As time passes, love is abandoned, and each goes off to find new lovers and new stimulation.

Eating mooncakes is exactly the same thing. Before it reaches the mouth, one imagines the sweetness of the mooncake, and one's mouth waters. While eating it, one's heart blossoms with sweetness, and the taste is endless. But once one is finished, those who deeply love it cannot help but pick up another and put it in their mouth. For those with a mediocre fondness for mooncakes, once one is finished, they let go of it. In short, once the mooncake is swallowed, everything is over.

Therefore, I admire even more the foresight of the founding ancestor of the mooncake, who actually made the mooncake perfectly fit all the conditions of the love relationships between men and women of today, hundreds of years later.

At the same time, the shape of the mooncake is round, resembling the bright moon on the night of the Mid-Autumn Festival. But how can the bright moon always be full? After the Mid-Autumn Festival, the moon wanes day by day. The mooncake's outer shape resembles the moon, and its inner filling resembles love. No wonder love can never last as long as the Mid-Autumn moon and cannot help but wane like the Mid-Autumn moon after Mid-Autumn.

Flowers cannot always be beautiful, the moon cannot always be round, and love cannot last forever without fading – all of these can be called "the fate of the mooncake"!

Swapping the Nest for Phoenixes 179

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 7: Brotherly Affection Conceals a Letter, Pitying a Weak Sister; Heavy with Poetic and Scholarly Air, Peeking Shadows Laugh at a Poor Scholar

His brother's face showed anger, sadness, and distress, but it was impossible to know for sure. Wuxuan waited for him to calm down for a while before saying, "Elder sister, don't misunderstand. I called you here to give you this letter because it was purely out of good intentions." Menglan remained silent. Wuxuan said, "I'm sorry, I opened the letter and read it. But based on the language in the letter, it seems that you haven't met this Mr. Zhang yet." Menglan used all her strength and barely managed to utter a "yes." Wuxuan said, "Weren't you out yesterday afternoon? Wang Ma received this letter and took it directly to Father. I was dozing nearby and saw clearly that it was a letter for you, so I lied and snatched it away. Fortunately, this letter didn't fall into Father's hands, or it would have been terrible." Menglan slightly bowed her waist and seemed to murmur a "thank you, elder brother." Wuxuan said, "I sympathize with your situation, but I can't help you much. So, since you are only corresponding with him, I can't bring myself to object. Moreover, I know this Mr. Zhang, and he is a mature scholar for his age. If you befriend him, his literary expression will surely comfort you. And I also believe he won't have any immoral behavior. I congratulate you on having such a friend." Menglan didn't know if he was speaking ironically or sincerely, and her heart was still pounding wildly. But quickly, she looked up at Wuxuan and saw that his expression was very calm and didn't seem angry. So, she said in a low voice, "Although what I did was wrong, I had no choice. Because Mr. Zhang keeps writing to me, and I can't refuse. The words in his letters are very generous, and we, as women with new knowledge, can't completely dismiss him. Besides, what he says really touches my heart. Elder brother, please forgive me." (85)

World News

A Glimpse of the Kabuki-za Theater in Tokyo 180

— Jiyun

In Japan's current economic boom, various forms of entertainment are naturally beyond imagination. The Kabuki-za is the largest theater in Tokyo, competing with the Takarazuka Revue. It usually performs classical plays, sometimes interspersed with modern dramas. Japanese classical plays are very similar to China's Peking Opera, with profound lyrics and abstract performances, which young people cannot understand. Chinese people can only watch their modern dramas; otherwise, the grotesque masks and the unsightly appearance of long swords and bare feet in the classical plays are truly a headache. The prices at the Kabuki-za range from fifty cents to four yen, more than ten times more expensive than movies. The audience is mostly from the middle class and above. In Japan, before a middle-class family gets engaged, the man and woman must first meet each other, so the Kabuki-za's lounge has become a place for meetings.

The architecture of the Kabuki-za is completely in the Japanese palace style on the outside. The cheapest fifty-cent tickets can only enter and exit through the side door, fully demonstrating its class concept. Tickets are sold a week in advance, and customers can choose their seats themselves and enter according to the number. There are no empty seats on holidays and Sundays. The stage is shallow and wide. Contrary to China, there are therefore more seats. The clapper sounds to open the curtain, and the stage is lit with electric lights to indicate the time of day and night. During performances and dialogues, music and onomatopoeia are often used, like in sound movies. Modern dramas are mostly comedies and tragedies, and the performances are more moving and easier to understand. The audience listens quietly without making noise, and the architecture is very reasonable, so every word and phrase on stage can be clearly understood by the audience. There is no music during breaks, and viewers use this time to attend to rest and smoke. When scenery is being set up inside the curtain, the sound of hammering is constant, and it is very time-consuming. In Japanese theatrical customs, famous actors must appear on stage repeatedly every night, performing several scenes. Sometimes, due to excessive fatigue, they have to play some supporting roles to make up the numbers. So, being a famous actor in Japan is very hard work. Also, if a customer has met an actor before, they can send a business card to the backstage during the performance for a visit. Then, tea, snacks, and candies are sent out to reciprocate the customer's support, which is also very unique.

Pu Yi visited the Kabuki-za to see a play when he traveled to Japan last year. So, the theater set up a temporary lounge for him, which has been preserved to this day and is called the "Imperial Seat," which is great for advertising. The lounge is attached to a shop, like a department store, with Chinese, Western, and Japanese food available. Because Japanese plays start at 4:00 PM and last until late at night, it is necessary to have meals in the theater. In the past, people ate lunch boxes, but now there is a dining room, which is very convenient. In addition to the dining room, various shops sell all kinds of sundries, with cosmetics and actresses' photos as souvenirs. There is also an exhibition displaying manuscript drafts of scripts, illustrations, the author's life, stage settings, and plot fragments, so the audience has another place to relax. A temporary nursery and a photo studio are located in the basement. The nursery has children's beds and is supervised by caregivers. This is very convenient for women with babies. The noise and chaos in Chinese theaters, which make people feel uncomfortable, must be improved and prevented.

Feature

Scenery of Shamian 181

— Wang Zhen

Guangzhou's Shamian has not received much attention in the decade or so since the Shameen Incident occurred in 1925, but recently, because Generalissimo Chiang Kai-shek visited the British Consulate on Shamian from the Whampoa gunboat, this place has rekindled people's memories.

Due to the Shameen Incident, Shamian has left a very frightening and negative impression on people in general. However, if we put aside all political views and focus on Shamian itself, we can come to the opposite conclusion.

Indeed, Shamian is quite moving. It is a sandbar next to Shameen, with an area of no more than one or two hundred acres. It is only a short distance from the Shameen Embankment, separated by a narrow river channel. In peacetime, this river channel is filled with yachts exclusively for people to enjoy.

"Take a river cruise!" the boat women sitting on the shore entice passersby with seductive glances.

Shameen and the embankment are completely a bustling street. People who are not used to the hustle and bustle may feel suffocated when they come here for a walk, but if you stroll across the exquisite stone bridge that spans the river channel to Shamian on the other side, you will definitely get a different feeling.

Here, there are smooth asphalt roads, and green lawns are scattered on both sides of the road. Near the riverbank, dozens of huge-trunked shrubs are neatly planted. When the branches and leaves are lush, the graceful shade covers the road. The sunlight shines through the gaps in the branches and leaves, forming countless small circles, like a beautiful pattern. Occasionally, a breeze blows, and the leaves rustle. The noise of Shameen and the embankment on the opposite bank is covered by this natural sound. In this short distance of ten or so feet, two completely different worlds are divided.

Many benches are placed on both sides of the road. When tired, you can sit down here. In the depths of the green shade, you can often see a corner of red wall, some of which are banks opened by Westerners, and some are Westerners' residences.

If you walk further, you will reach the embankment on the other side. In front of you is a vast river surface, which is the famous White Swan Pond since the Republic of China. The pond is very deep, and many foreign merchant ships and warships are anchored in the middle.

Every evening, you can see couples returning from the tennis courts, arm in arm, waving their light rackets, humming popular love songs. The sound of their synchronized footsteps gradually disappears with their figures.

At this time, you may also feel a different foreign atmosphere.

In any case, Shamian is beautiful and quite moving.

Grain: Flour Skyrockets and Hits Limit; All Months Rise by 1 Dime 189

Yesterday, the flour market was extremely excited, and the market had already reached its peak. The price of each month's product has been forced to halt price changes in the afternoon, because the stock exchange, based on the previous rule, dictated that the price could only be raised by 10% each day. This situation, not seen since last June, is now happening again. When the price was opened, due to the price of dripping wheat, it was also up 3 or 4 cents. Outside the industry, expectations were all unified, and this month's opening price was up 34 cents, and the long-term opening price was also up 23 cents. Afterward, due to greater buying, prices also rose slightly. By the time the afternoon session had opened, the situation changed drastically again. News had spread that customers were active, factories were compensating, and moreover prices on yarn and cotton as well as the exchange rate had risen. This led to enormous enthusiasm for buying. At the beginning, near term was only up two or three cents, but finally in March it hit three yuan, seven jiao, one fen, and seven li and a half (up a tenth from the day before). Thus, since the opening of this month, prices were all inflated to the point of maxing out the dime increase each time. The market has thus been set, and the stock exchange will wait until further resolution of the matter, and will thus reopen when possible.

Ultimately the price result rose from one tenth to one and seven tenths. Watching future steps, if the government is unable to create an affordable method, it is feared the price increase will not be stoppable. Nanyang, especially Guangzhou and Shantou, is the most greedy, and northern ocean Tianjin is also quite active. Yesterday, there was a trend of continued increase in the market. As the day reached its end, there were hot spots, and northerners actively bought He Xia geng rice, and Cantonese also competed to buy at high prices. The market began to stabilize. However, Shantou's consumption remains active. Northerners and Cantonese also continued to buy slightly, so the market's mood remained positive. A total of 3,460 packages of Gan rice were sold, 5,158 packages of Xiang rice, 220 packages of Jing xian, and 100 packages of factory xian, still totaling more than 10,000 packages.

Shanghai South's New Japonica Drop Has Already Stabilized 192

(Shanghai North) Yesterday, the sources from He Xia and other places continued to arrive, with a total of about 43 or 44 boats. The new japonica and Yang Dubu tip sold well in the market, while damaged japonica, old new Bian Yuan, and other goods were bland. The market price of damaged japonica continued to rise by several points to about a dime. The new japonica high-quality goods were fatigued by several points, and the middle position remained stable. There was no rise or fall in the new Yao species Yang Du tip. The old new Bian Yuan was bland and fatigued. The customer tip was firm.

(Shanghai South) Yesterday, the sources from various gangs were similar to before, with a total of 54 or 55 boats arriving, totaling 11,3400 shi of goods. The new japonica market condition initially showed signs of fatigue, but by noon, after the Tianjin gang took action and bought 1,5600 packages, the situation turned around and the price rose back by a dime. As for the new thin rice such as Yaozhong Baige, etc., due to sluggish sales, although the buyers from Qingdao, Yantai, and Dalian bought 1,6700 packages, and the thin damaged rice was over 100 packages, the resulting price was lower by a dime. The supply and demand of Du Jian was similar, with no rise or fall. The price of foreign Jian continued to fall by 1.2 dimes in the opposite direction. Thick and thin damaged rice showed slight signs of softening. The old new Bian Yuan was short of goods and had no market.

Special Feature: Decline in Japanese Cotton Cloth Exports (Continued from the 10th Day Report) 193

— Wang Jingshi

Exports to the Dutch East Indies in the first half of the year amounted to 1,679,960,000 yards, a decrease of 28,884,000 yards, or 14 percent. This is the second-largest outlet for Japanese cotton cloth, second only to British India. However, the changes in this trade are of a drastic nature, resulting from the deterioration of relations between Japan and the Netherlands. Exports to Egypt totaled 47,868,000 yards, a decrease of 28,613,000 yards, or 37.4 percent, compared to the same period last year. In July of last year, the Egyptian government announced a trade agreement with Japan, imposing a 40 percent countervailing duty on Japanese goods starting from September 20th. Subsequently, Japan and Egypt held negotiations in Cairo on October 20th of last year regarding the cancellation or modification of the countervailing duty, but the outcome was ultimately unsuccessful. The Egyptian cotton cloth market is actually Japan's fourth-largest outlet, its importance only falling behind the four Northeastern provinces.

Exports to Colombia were completely cut off this year, as the commercial agreement between Japan and Colombia was abolished on April 30th of last year. Subsequently, mutual benefits were restricted, leading to a cessation of trade. As for cotton cloth imported by Iran from Japan, the figure for last year was 23,820,000 yards, also a decrease of 3,507,000 yards, or 36.2 percent. This was due to the enactment of a new law in that region on May 22nd of last year, stipulating that all goods imported from Japan would be subject to an import duty of 15 percent ad valorem. Therefore, there is not much hope for the future of trade with that country. Exports to Cuba saw a percentage decrease as high as 97.9 percent, with a quantity of 9,636,000 yards, which is not insignificant. Cuba had also announced in March of last year the imposition of a 25 percent dumping duty on imports of Japanese cotton cloth and 100 percent on rayon. Recent negotiations between the two parties may lead to an agreement on a minimum tariff rate for Japanese goods, provided that Japan imports half the export value from Cuba.

Furthermore, concerning Argentina, a South American country, the quantity of Japanese cotton cloth exported during the first half of the year was 45,353,000 yards, a decrease of 16 percent, which is more unfavorable compared to England. Moreover, the country's export association has stipulated that a 5 percent control tax be levied on imported goods to subsidize exports. Similarly, exports to Haiti in North America have also decreased by 75 percent, mainly due to a 100 percent increase in tariff rates. In El Salvador, 20 years ago, 9 million yards of cotton cloth were imported from Japan. Subsequently, effective measures were taken to limit its import, thus reducing the figure to 170,000 yards. This method is attributed to the strict imposition of a 200 percent import duty, while simultaneously reducing the tariff on local exports by 25 percent. These are the facts of the past two years.

Regarding Australia, there has been no significant change in the past six months. However, the new tariff regulations in May stipulate that cotton cloth imports are subject to a 70 to 110 percent ad valorem tariff. Consequently, Japan is set to lose a significant market in Australia. Therefore, Japan is currently boycotting Australian wool in retaliation.

As for exports to the Dutch East Indies, a total of 249,589,000 yards were exported in the six months of this year. The amount to date has not changed much. During the previous trade year, from October of last year to March of this year, exports and re-exports from Japan exceeded 7,420,000 yards. However, the commercial agreement of the previous year was interrupted in March, and negotiations resumed in July of last year. At that time, Britain paid close attention to the progress of Japanese cotton cloth, resulting in the Indian authorities increasing taxes by 5 percent. As for Hong Kong, a free trade port with no import restrictions, imports totaled 40,399,000 yards in the first half of the year, a sharp increase of 65.3 percent compared to the same period last year. However, a portion of this was re-exported elsewhere. Imports from Japan to Northeast China reached 106,895,000 yards, an increase of 21,982,000 yards, or 25.9 percent, compared to the same period. At the same time, the Kwantung Leased Territory also saw an increase of 44 percent, with the increase undoubtedly being transshipped to central China.

In summary, the exports of Japanese cotton cloth are generally trending downwards. However, there has been an increase in Europe, although various countries on the European continent have increased tariffs due to their different characteristics to protect their own industries. Japan, on the other hand, has separately signed preferential treatment agreements. Therefore, the prospects for further increases, except for Germany, seem promising.

Finance Stock Market Loosening, Bullish Bidding Ultimately Unsustainable, Several Reversals Mid-Course... Final Result Still a Drop of Two Jiao 194

Yesterday's gold market saw a slight increase in pure gold, but ultimately remained suppressed. Despite swap pressures, buying interest was still strong, with frequent rebounds mid-course. However, the stock market weakened, leading to a final decline. In the early morning, overseas silver markets saw London level, the U.S. halt, and New York and Montevideo commercial markets all suspend trading. Exchange rates opened slightly higher, with London's raw gold rising half a penny. The Central Bank's listed prices showed both British and American currencies unchanged, and the customs gold unit remained stable. The standard bid price was listed as rising to 1154 yuan. Off-exchange pre-market trading opened at around 574 yuan. Fuxing, Yongda, Decheng, Yuanmao, Yongheng, and others were selling, leading to a weakening trend. The morning opening was slightly higher, but due to increased bullish activity, it briefly rebounded. However, the citizens have experienced the lessons of January 28th, and the stationing of troops across the border has become commonplace. What better way do these frightened citizens have other than "avoiding"?

Due to "avoiding disaster," we are even more reminded of the news published in the newspaper a few days ago (perhaps it was the newspaper on Double Ten Day?) about a young girl committing suicide by jumping into the sea. That young lady was afraid of the ravages of the ×× people, and thought that she would die sooner or later, so in the midst of "avoiding disaster," she generously jumped into the sea to preserve her "pure body." The behavior of this young lady is naturally opposed by us, and the cause of her death, in addition to the "national crisis," also has remnants of the Jianyu rebellion nesting behind it. However, because of this, we can also see that in the serious national crisis, the people are unable to be happy under the torment of real pain, and they naturally have no mood to force a smile. It is like "being slapped in the face and then smiling."

Perhaps some people will say that great undertakings must be completed with a happy mood. Like the current self-disturbing ordinary people who are panicked all day long, they can only disrupt their steps. In the current extraordinary period, we should calmly cope with all incidents. This is correct, but it does not mean indulging in pleasure, let alone whitewashing peace. The result of indulging in pleasure and whitewashing peace is only worse than lacking self-confidence, because lacking self-confidence at least sees the current serious situation, while indulging in pleasure and whitewashing peace only wants to cover up and evade the serious situation.

The Muleteer Group 213

— Jin Ge

"Old Li, where's that handkerchief?" It was still the sweaty one asking.

"Why are you asking about her?"

"Why be stingy? Isn't it just an empty cock?"

It was still last night, staying at the horse inn in Dongkoujing. The daughter of the innkeeper was very pretty, her feet were so small and stylish, her eyes were dark and charming, and she even had a beautiful bun. Somehow, Old Li got his hands on her. When he left this morning, she asked Old Li when he would come again. Old Li himself didn't know when he would come here again, so the young girl cried, and Old Li took her soaked handkerchief as a souvenir!

The sweaty one went to sleep angrily, and Old Li also went to sleep boredly.

They surrounded the cargo shelves in a circle, people slept close to the shelves, and firewood was collected in the middle, burning all night. This is called "fire group" (Note 3), watched over by the brothers in turn.

Fatigue brought them one by one into dreamland, a sweet sleep;

The next day, before the sky was bright and refreshing, the lead-blue sky was hanging with residual stars, and the earth was dark and gray. They had already tied up their horses and embarked on their distant journey again.

Still that dark group, they were still singing happily:

"Going from Sichuan to Guizhou,"

"Seen so many young girls,"

Note: In the mountains of Southwest China, there are owners of thousands of tall mules and horses who hire those strong young men from declining rural areas. Those young men run east and west with those mules and horses every day, earning money for their owners. These young men are called "muleteers."

Note two: "Kai Shao" they call rest as kai shao.

Note three: "Fire group" is used to scare away tigers and to keep warm.

Rumors 214

— Mu Ye

Early in the morning, San Mazi's teahouse was already full of people. Everyone's face was so tense, looking very uncomfortable, as if everyone was angry with someone, all depressed there, motionless, without a sound. Everyone was like a piece of wood, only pairs of eyeballs, staring blankly at each other a few times, and nothing else.

Usually, San Mazi always squeaked and screamed. Today, he also changed his usual habits, as if it was the first day he opened a teahouse. Everything was stiff and awkward. He himself couldn't figure out why half of a spoonful of water would be poured outside the pot. He had a ghost in his stomach like everyone else. He was worried that one day ××'s plane would really fly to this village, and maybe drop a "thousand-pound" bomb specifically to bomb his small teahouse, which would be terrible!

"Hey, Shopkeeper Jia is here, isn't that..."

The bald man sitting under the window by the east wall said quietly. Judging from his expression, he tried to lower his voice as much as possible, as if he was afraid of being heard. But everyone had already focused their attention on Shopkeeper Jia of the Zhenxing Rice Store. Everyone gestured to each other with their eyes. San Mazi raised his chin at the bald man and pursed his lips.

In this way, under the gaze of the crowd, Shopkeeper Jia hurried in. He wiped his sweat with his sleeve, and gestured with his hand in front of his face, and said as soon as he opened his mouth:

"It's over, it's over,...it's damn over..."

Everyone had a premonition of what "it's over" meant. The bald man almost didn't cry. San Mazi's legs were shaking. He expected that the "thousand-pound" bomb was definitely unavoidable. He slowly walked over. Shopkeeper Jia was gesturing and talking:

"...What else is there to say? I heard that the fighting will start not today, but tomorrow, anyway, it won't be more than five days at most! This time is not like that time!...Yesterday I went to the city, the shops were all closed, and there wasn't even a ghost on the street..."

"Are we going to give him a hard time?" a young man asked like this.

"How would our family know? I think it's... Anyway, this matter is hard to say! Their troops come every day, and their warships are full of people on the harbor..."

"The plane is going to drop bombs - "thousand-pound" ones?" San Mazi couldn't help but ask.

"Hmph, thousand-pound ones! Let me tell you, those are still the grandchildren's generation! In short! This time it will be a hundred times more powerful than last time!"

Everyone was stunned, and countless sighs rose in the silence. Everyone was intimidated by Shopkeeper Jia's words.

"Hey! Don't worry about anything else, it's important to get something to eat! Whether we fight or not, we still have to eat! I spent a lot of effort and only got five hundred shi of rice..." Shopkeeper Jia raised his voice and said to everyone: "If you want to prepare something to eat, please do it early!" Saying that, he left the small teahouse.

The bald man was the first to follow out in a hurry.

So everyone took this shocking news that the fighting would start in five

Page 18

days to all directions of this village.

The next day, San Mazi really had no intention to do business anymore. Before dawn, he took down the Qingxin Teahouse sign that was hanging high. At lunchtime, he rushed to the Zhenxing Rice Store to find Shopkeeper Jia.

"Hey, Shopkeeper Jia, let's get a bag of rice too, so we don't have nothing to eat when we fight..."

"I told you to come early, didn't I? Isn't it already sold out? Just wait, I've already sent someone to the city to pick up rice. Just wait and see what happens!" Shopkeeper Jia pointed to the rice warehouse and said like this. There was a smile in his voice.

Five days passed quickly. It was already the morning of the seventh day. Everyone was like a rat coming out of its hole, sneaking around everywhere to inquire about news. San Mazi was the first to bump into Shopkeeper Jia:

"Ah, why isn't, isn't the fighting starting!"

Shopkeeper Jia touched his shaved chin and said with a smile:

"Probably, probably it's a rumor...!"

Storm 215

— Qi Ying

—Mountain Walking Notes Six

During the half-month of mountain walking in Dalong Mountain, what we can't forget the most is the day we left Old Ma Fu's house. We felt that the journey was short, and it would only take half a day to reach the foot of the mountain. So everyone wanted to walk again and didn't want to ride horses. Moreover, our horsemanship was not very good. Maybe when going down the slope, if the horse lost its footing, we wouldn't be able to hold the reins, and there would be a danger of falling into the valley with the horse.

When we left Old Ma Fu's house, the sky was so clear; when the blood-red sun rushed out from behind the eastern mountain range, it used its strong light to tightly grasp this mountain road, as if it was going to steam oil out of the land piece by piece. Looking down from the mountain peak, every mountain stone was reflected by the sunlight so brightly that it was dazzling, and the valleys on both sides of the path were smoky. Because it was early morning, wisps of cool breeze could still drift down from the mountain peaks from time to time. We didn't feel any threat at all, and we sang mountain songs softly as we walked.

Unconsciously, we gradually reached the middle of the mountain. The sunlight gradually left us, and everything at the foot of the mountain gradually became clear. Everyone's hearts were happy. At some point, the sky suddenly changed, and dark clouds rolled over, as if a giant black hand of a demon was about to stretch out and tightly crush the mountain peak. We realized that the storm was about to come. So we quickened our pace, but the foot of the mountain was still far away from us, and the valleys on both sides seemed even more gloomy and empty. In the middle of the mountain, except for the four of us, there was no other living creature. Not only our hearts were trembling, but also the trees and mountain stones by the roadside seemed to be gradually destroyed by the wind rolling down from the mountain peaks and trembled and shrunk. In this gloomy mountainside, they were probably shivering in terror like us! The whole mountainside was caught in the grip of terror.

At this time, we actively wanted to find a place to hide by the roadside, but unfortunately there was not even a large mountain stone. We had no choice but to lift our weak steps and move forward. Suddenly, at the turning point in the middle of the mountain, a thatched cottage appeared near one side of the mountain. Judging by its appearance, it was a small teahouse. Outside the house, a woman who looked about twenty years old and a little girl with two braids, who was six or seven years old, stood in the middle of the road, looking anxiously at the foot of the mountain, as if waiting for someone to return.

We were as happy as if we had discovered a new continent, and walked up quickly. The middle-aged woman heard the footsteps and hurriedly turned around. She looked at us in surprise. Probably seeing that we were not bad people, she calmed down and asked, "Gentlemen, are you going down the mountain? The weather is bad, and the storm is coming soon. Why don't you have a cup of tea here before you go?" Saying that, she turned around again and glanced at the foot of the mountain, and then walked down to the shed and brewed a pot of tea for each of us. Then, she went to the middle of the road to look at the foot of the mountain.

As soon as we sat down, the storm came suddenly. They roared and wailed, carrying threats and intimidation. The valleys echoed with a booming sound, and waterfalls poured down in the valleys, as if the heavens and the earth were competing. The shed and the tables in the shed were whistling in the wind, as if heavy footsteps were passing by. We all hurried to hide in the house. The middle-aged woman took the hand of the six- or seven-year-old girl and stood at the door, complaining to us, "Gentlemen, such a strong wind and rain often blow travelers into the valley. This girl's father," she glanced at the girl who was about to cry, "He went down the mountain early in the morning to sell firewood, and he hasn't returned yet. Could something have happened?" Saying that, she sobbed softly.

When we heard her words, everyone looked at each other in panic. We squeezed our bodies even closer.

The sound of the wind and rain outside the house became stronger. We all silently prayed in our hearts that the traveler would be safe!

Camel 216

— Zhu Lu

In the early morning of the northern country, the sky is hazy, and the blue sky is boundless, covering the silent and dead earth.

In the hazy mist, a group of camels walked slowly, beside them a man holding a whip, holding a rope tied to the camel's nose, walking step by step, leaving a trail of hoof prints in the sand.

The camels' backs were loaded with bags of coal, they plodded step by step, and the bells in their necks rang as they swung.

The camels' sleepy eyes looked particularly depressed. In their eyes, there seemed to be shadows of dozens of generations struggling in the desert, inherited from generation to generation. In their humps, the thick manes were covered with countless winds and sands. On their thin legs, there were scars from being whipped. They seemed to be enduring a lot of grief and indignation, swaying and walking in the sand.

A group of camels plodded slowly beside the tall ancient city, swaying as they stepped on the rubble on the ground. They seemed to be thinking, thinking about the wild life they had lived in the desert in the past, thinking about the brutality of being whipped when they were bound, thinking about carrying many heavy things, being led by the nose by others...

A man, pulling the head of a leading camel, led a group of burdened camels towards the solemn city gate.

The sky brightened, and the sunlight of the morning glow shone through the floating clouds. The warm light shone on a group of camels, casting long shadows diagonally on the ground.

The camels' eyes, accustomed to the darkness, were somewhat dizzy by the sunlight. They tried their best to open their eyes wide, looking at the warm and bright light in the late autumn...

They were excited by the stimulation of the sunlight. The courage that had disappeared from their whole bodies surged up again. Their bodies felt warm, they raised their steps high and walked excitedly.

They seemed to be thinking about the exciting life in the desert, the free days, and the situation of fighting against the wind and sand... They seemed to be fascinated, and a kind of yearning was growing. They were yearning for that freedom, that sand man, that wind!...

The camels were struggling.

The camels' monkey-like heads shook, they opened their lips to bite, a burst of heat came out, and saliva flowed from their mouths. They got rid of the heavy burden on their backs, and roared stubbornly in the sunlight...

They bravely raised their heads and ran towards the sunlight.

Several enthusiastic theater movement comrades have come together. The failure to improve the broadcasting methods and the unrealistic dubbing technology are the two major fatal injuries. The society can use the latest broadcasting methods, and hire professional dubbing talents who are fluent in Mandarin and have rich experience. Mr. Bao Mingshan, a famous harmonica expert in our country, previously accepted an invitation from the Anding Radio Station to teach and play world-famous songs on the station every Sunday. Now, starting from this Sunday (the 18th), he will continue to teach and play the harmonica at the Youlian Radio Station (frequency 880) every Sunday morning from 10:30 to 11:30. Demanding a Public Performance of "Fight for Kiev" 223

Editor Sir:

I have always admired your enthusiasm for promoting the film culture industry. I think that I have a request now that you, sir, will surely convey for me!

Not long ago, the Soviet ambassador to China invited people from all walks of life in Shanghai to watch the Soviet military documentary "Fight for Kiev." I also went to see it at that time. Sir, when I saw the Red Army on the screen fighting bravely to defend their motherland, my almost frozen blood immediately boiled.

"Kiev" is a city in the Soviet Union close to Western European imperialism. It is a target for all imperialists to attack the Soviet Union. "Fight for Kiev" is a film about the Soviet Union simulating an imperialist attack on "Kiev" and the Red Army rising up to resist. The entire film shows that the only way for a country to be invaded is to resist, because only resistance can defend the territory.

In the eyes of X imperialism, China is full of "Kievs." Under their threats and temptations, China's "Kievs" have been lost one after another. But there are still many "Kievs" left. X imperialism's insatiable ambition will naturally have to attack. For our own survival and the survival of the country, how can we keep the "Kievs" that have not been lost, or how can we take back the "Kievs" that have already been lost from the hands of X imperialism? I think that what "Fight for Kiev" tells us is absolutely correct.

China has reached a critical juncture of survival and death. We will launch all forces that can resist X and save the country. The cultural world and the literary and artistic world have all taken on extraordinary responsibilities. Film, this weapon of propaganda, we naturally cannot fail to use it. Then, we have reason to demand that "Fight for Kiev," which can promote the unity of the masses to resist war, be shown publicly.

I hope that you, sir, will publish this letter in the newspaper. I hope that the Shanghai Grand Theater, which specializes in showing Soviet films, can find a way to show "Fight for Kiev" in a short period of time. I think that there are more people who have such expectations than just me!

Wishing you peace!

Supplement to the Shanghai Shenbao, Automobile Special Issue

The Successful Struggle of German Industrial Giant Bosch Over Fifty Years 224

The German city of Wu-tun-bao has beautiful scenery. The mountains and rivers are picturesque. It is difficult to count the great figures from all walks of life who have been produced there throughout history. If one must briefly mention their names, they are Schiller, Zeppelin, and Daimler. Since Wu-tun-bao is blessed with the spirit of its mountains and rivers, and produces outstanding people, it is not surprising that the name of a farmer's son by the Swabian River changed in the late nineteenth century into a household name. However, the reason why this farmer's son achieved such a great reputation was not due to any unprecedented invention or any great achievement. The only reason was that the goods he sold to the world were all outstanding and of the highest quality. This is truly remarkable. Who is this farmer's son? It is Robert Bosch, who is known throughout the world. Bosch was born seventy-five years ago, on September 23, 1861, in the village of Albeck on the Swabian River. The new thoroughfare from Stuttgart to Ulm to Munich passes through Bavaria.

The childhood anecdotes of famous figures throughout history are almost always fascinating. But Bosch had no special traits in his youth that would indicate that he would achieve such great fame in the future. The town of Ulm, located on the banks of the picturesque and mirror-like Danube River, has a small school. It was where he studied as a child. Ulm has a famous craftsman named Meyer. He apprenticed with him and became a fine mechanic. After completing his apprenticeship, he worked as a plumber, machinist, and mechanical engineer for several years. Then he joined the Ulm Pioneer Corps and served in the military. After his discharge, he returned to his old profession. During this period, he worked as an electrical mechanic at the Escherich factory in Nuremberg, and diligently studied electrical engineering at the Stuttgart Advanced School. Then he went to the United States and was hired by the Bergmann factory as an electrical engineer. It was at this time that he became acquainted with Edison. He then left his job and was hired by the London branch of Siemens for six months. Later, in 1886, when Bosch was twenty-five years old, his workshop in Stuttgart was successfully established. There was one skilled assistant and one apprentice in the workshop, so the scale was small. However, this was the starting point of Bosch's life's work. He had a firm goal and worked diligently and consistently to achieve it. Throughout his life, he never relied on publicity, and there was no need to rely on publicity. His hard work and arduous efforts resulted in achievements that were his best advertising material.

Everything starts simple and ends great. Bosch's success was no different. A mechanical engineer needed an electrical igniter for a gas-powered engine. He asked Bosch to find a way to make one. So he started to make it to meet his needs. And his amazing progress and success in the industrial world began with this. When gasoline-powered engines became popular all over the world, Bosch's name also became well-known. At that time, the electrical magneto that Bosch had carefully created for this type of engine was in high demand and indispensable. So even if people didn't want Bosch's name to be known, it was impossible. (To be continued)

European and American Automobile Information 225

— Yu

Small Cars Are Popular in Europe Due to the high price of gasoline in Europe, several types of small cars are popular this summer. One of the best is said to be the "Flying Fox 500." It is the latest model. It can travel 47 miles per gallon of gasoline. The most expensive gasoline in Europe sells for $1.16 per gallon. It is most economical to buy this new type of fuel-efficient car. Even in places where the price of gasoline is the lowest, at 40 cents or more per gallon, it is still a good deal. The new Flying Fox has a streamlined shape and sells for $700. The whole body is made of metal. It is equipped with safety glass and four-wheel hydraulic brakes. Much thought has been given to safe driving.

July Sales of American Cars The sales of American cars in July were very strong. Both production and sales improved. Chevrolet sold a total of 3,926 passenger cars and trucks in New York City in July, a record high. In the same month of 1935, the number was 2,542. The July sales of the Lincoln Zephyr were 1,503, the second-best sales month since the new car was launched ten months ago. Sales in April were 1,607, and sales in May were 1,500. From January 1 to August 10, the retail sales of Walters Mabe were 133,155, a record high. This is an increase of 27% over the same period last year. Studebeck sold 5,348 passenger cars and trucks in July, bringing the total sales for the first seven months of this year to 43,512, which is more than the sales for the twelve months of 1935. The sales of Cadillac LaSalle increased by 33% compared to July of last year. The retail sales of Graham in July increased by 20% compared to the same month last year.

Dodge's Used Car Promotion Plan Dodge, a division of Chrysler Corporation, recently announced a used car promotion plan. This plan includes both passenger cars and trucks. This plan is called "Blue Seal of Approval." Any used car that has been inspected by the dealer and guaranteed for its appearance, mechanical parts, and fairness of price will be marked with a blue seal on the car. According to Mr. Xilin, director of Dodge's used car sales department, the company's dealers sold a total of 371,237 used cars in the first seven months of this year.

The Songjiang-Songjiang-Sijing Road is Open for Passenger Transport 226

— Cao Wenhai

The Brick-Yu Branch Line Also Opened on the 10th

The Songjiang-Songjiang Automobile Company was founded by Mr. Niu Yongjian and Mr. Yin Shisheng. The company has been established for five years. Passengers have praised its convenience. Four years ago, the company opened another Songjiang-Sijing Road and started construction. It has now been opened to traffic after three years. However, passengers must travel to the Xindongmen Station in Songjiang. To get to Shanghai or Sijing, you need to change cars. The original plan was to go directly from "Sijing, Qibao" to "Shanghai." Then, the distance between Songjiang and Shanghai can be shortened by one-third compared to the current route. It only takes less than an hour to get there. According to the records, Songjiang County was called Songjiang Prefecture during the Qing Dynasty. It governed the territory of seven counties. Its elegant scenery is best known for the Nine Peaks and Three Rivers. And the best of the Nine Peaks is "Yu Mountain." Farmers build houses and live around the foot of the mountain in the forests of trees, forming a small market. The shops also have "teahouses, restaurants, and grocery stores," etc. However, their scale is not large. There are no hotels. On the top of the West Mountain, there is a Catholic church. Every year in May, the church holds a grand ceremony to welcome the Virgin. At this time, Catholics from far and near come to the mountain to pray. But this road can only be accessed by water. Taking a small boat takes a lot of time. Round trips are not very convenient. Mr. Yin Shisheng, the owner of the Songjiang-Shanghai Automobile Company, for the convenience of travelers, opened a branch line at the "Brick Bridge" station in Qingxian after the opening of the Songjiang-Sijing Road (Songjiang to Sijing). It goes directly to "Yu Mountain." The road has now been opened to traffic on National Day. The timetables for the two routes are listed below for passengers' reference.

(1) Songjiang-Songjiang Timetable Take the bus from the Shanghai-Minhang Long-Distance Bus Company in the Guohuo Road behind the South Railway Station in Shanghai. The first bus departs at 8:15 AM. The second bus departs at 9:15 AM. The third bus departs at 10:15 AM. The fourth bus departs at 11:15 AM. The first bus departs at 1:15 PM. The second bus departs at 2:15 PM. The third bus departs at 3:15 PM. The fourth bus departs at 4:15 PM. The last bus departs at 5:15 PM. There are four buses departing from Shanghai to Songjiang in the morning. There are five buses in the afternoon. There are a total of nine buses per day.

(2) Songjiang-Shanghai Timetable Departures from Songjiang to Shanghai. The first bus departs at 7:00 AM. The second bus departs at 8:00 AM. The third bus departs at 9:00 AM. The fourth bus departs at 10:00 AM. The last bus departs at 11:00 AM. The first bus departs at 1:00 PM. The second bus departs at 2:00 PM. The third bus departs at 3:00 PM. The last bus departs at 4:00 PM. Every Monday, the early bus from Songjiang to Shanghai is one hour earlier, departing at 7:00 AM. The full fare from Songjiang to Shanghai is 70 cents per person. Round-trip tickets are valid for one week from the date of issue. Passengers who purchase round-trip tickets cannot get on or off at intermediate stations, otherwise, the ticket will be void.

(3) Songjiang-Sijing Road Timetable Departures from the Xindongmen Station in Songjiang. The first bus departs at 7:30 AM. The second bus departs at 8:30 AM. The third bus departs at 10:30 AM. The last bus departs at 11:30 AM. The first bus departs at 1:30 PM. The second bus departs at 3:30 PM. The third bus departs at 4:30 PM. The last bus departs at 5:30 PM.

(4) Sijing to Songjiang Timetable Departures from the Henan Bridge in the Central Market of Sijing. The first bus departs at 7:30 AM. The second bus departs at 8:30 AM. The third bus departs at 9:30 AM. The last bus departs at 11:30 AM. The first bus departs at 12:30 PM. The second bus departs at 2:30 PM. The third bus departs at 4:30 PM. The last bus departs at 5:30 PM. The full fare from Sijing to Shanghai is 80 cents per person. The round-trip ticket is $1.25. The round-trip ticket is valid for one week from the date of issue. It will be void after the expiration date.

(5) Brick-Yu-Qian Combined Transport Timetable Departures from Shanghai to Brick Bridge. The Shanghai-Brick Bridge special bus departs at 8:30 AM. The Shanghai-Brick Bridge combined transport bus departs at 9:15 AM. Connects with the Songjiang-Sijing 10:30, 2 bus at the Xindongmen Station. Brick Bridge to Yu Mountain. Connects with the Shanghai-Brick Bridge 8:30 special bus at 10:30 AM. Connects with the Shanghai-Songjiang-Brick Bridge 9:15 combined transport bus at 11:00 AM. Yu Mountain to Brick Bridge. Connects with the Sijing 3:30 Brick-Songjiang to Shanghai 4:30 bus at 2:00 PM. Connects with the Brick-Shanghai special electric bus at 4:00 PM. Brick Bridge to Shanghai. Connects with the Shanghai bus departing from the Songjiang Central Station at 4:00 PM at 3:30 PM. Brick-Shanghai special bus at 5:00 PM. The timetable is for the speedboat connection to Yu Mountain. Since the completion of the Brick-Yu line on October 10, it has been opened to traffic. There are eight buses a day. It is reported that the Catholics in Yu Mountain have requested a special Shanghai-Yu special bus on Sunday. The company has also agreed to open a special bus.
